Here are the key findings:\n\n## Recent Enrollment Data\n\nAs of December 2024, across 29 states tracked, Medicaid managed care enrollment was 61.7 million, down by 3.6 million (-5.5%) year-over-year. Since April 2023, Medicaid enrollment has been on a downward trajectory as states complete eligibility redeterminations after the end of the COVID-19 public health emergency.\n\n## CMS and Policy Updates\n\nIn May, CMS revised the regulations governing state contracting with MCOs, with provisions intended to improve access and quality, including additional requirements relating to transparency about MCO performance. CMS issued a 5-year Medicaid integrity plan that identifies managed care as \"a critical priority for CMS' program integrity work during FYs 2024 – 2028\".\n\n## MCO Program Evolution\n\nIn April, Oklahoma launched mandatory managed care for children, parents, pregnant women, and expansion adults, making it the 41st state (plus DC) to contract with MCOs for the delivery of Medicaid services. CMS maintains the cost report data in the Healthcare Provider Cost Reporting Information System (HCRIS).\n\n## Data System and Access\n\nHCRIS includes data for the Hospital Cost Report (CMS-2552-96 and CMS-2552-10), Skilled Nursing Facility Cost Report (CMS-2540-96 and CMS-2540-10), Home Health Agency Cost Report (CMS-1728-94 and CMS-1728-94), Renal Facility Cost Report (CMS-265-94 and CMS-265-11), Health Clinic Cost Report (CMS-222-92), Hospice Cost Report (CMS-1984-99 and CMS-1984-14), Federally Qualified Health Clinic Cost Report (CMS-224-14), Rural Health Center Cost Report (CMS-222-17), Community Mental Health Center Cost Report (CMS-2088-92 and CMS-2088-17) and Organ Procurement Organizations(CMS-216-94).\n\n## Public Use Files\n\nThe Hospital Cost Report Public Use File (Hospital Cost Report PUF) presents select measures provided by hospitals through their annual cost report, and is organized at the hospital level. The Hospital Cost Report PUF is available for 2014 - 2018 at https://data.cms.gov/provider-compliance/cost-report/hospital-provider-cost-report.\n\n## Coverage\n\nA database of more than 6,000 hospitals is built from Medicare cost report information obtained from the federal Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) for all reporting periods since 1996.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"5bbccdf7-8abc-4087-a72d-94de712b06ca","timestamp":"2026-03-22T06:19:04.900Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"f8d7086a-8b14-4fd6-8766-8d1409465a15","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS","sessionId":"fe36a5fb-a2bc-4eb6-b6f8-8a2ba119fc51","version":"2.1.78","gitBranch":"main","slug":"federated-percolating-pnueli"}

{"parentUuid":"d056ebc1-59e9-4092-8051-fe86600b0b7b","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"ac3debdd0279c2c1f","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01HoNnWfhMXbqocGMzsZBprd","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_016n3UsogPrmEJK2abHKtQK2","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS/.claude/docs/research-oracle-health-market-sizing-sources-2026-03-22.md","content":"# Research Packet: Oracle Health Market Sizing Data Sources\n**Date**: 2026-03-22\n**Researcher**: Research Agent (Claude Sonnet 4.6)\n**Purpose**: Identify publicly available data sources, reports, and datasets for market sizing across three Oracle Health domains\n\n---\n\n## Research Question\n\nWhat publicly available market sizing data sources — containing actual numbers, enrollment figures, spending benchmarks, and market sizes — exist for Oracle Health's three primary domains: Payer (Health Insurance Technology), Revenue Cycle Management, and Provider (Health Systems / EHR)?\n\n---\n\n## Scope Boundaries\n\n**In scope:**\n- Publicly accessible or purchasable market research reports with specific TAM/SAM figures\n- Government datasets (CMS, ONC, AHA) with free enrollment and utilization data\n- Public company filings with revenue data usable for competitor benchmarking\n- Industry association benchmarks (HFMA, AHIP, KFF) with standardized metrics\n- Analyst firm forecasts (Grand View Research, MarketsandMarkets, KLAS, Mordor Intelligence)\n\n**Out of scope:**\n- Proprietary primary research (hospital IT assessments, individual health system interviews)\n- Consulting firm deliverables not available publicly\n- Internal Oracle Health data\n- SAM/SOM calculations (methodology only, not data)\n\n---\n\n## Canonical Definitions\n\n**TAM (Total Addressable Market)**: Total revenue opportunity if a vendor captured 100% of a market segment. Used here as market size figures from analyst reports.\n\n**SAM (Serviceable Addressable Market)**: Subset of TAM that a specific vendor's product can actually serve given geography, customer type, and product fit.\n\n**Unit Economics Method**: TAM = (number of potential customers) x (average spend per customer). Requires both a customer count source and a spending benchmark source.\n\n**Competitor Benchmark Method**: TAM estimated by summing or extrapolating from known public company revenues (R1 RCM, Waystar, Epic, etc.).\n\n**CMS Risk Adjustment**: Federal program through which MA plans receive capitated payments adjusted by member health status using Hierarchical Condition Categories (HCC). CMS paid ~$140B in MA risk-adjusted benchmarks in 2023.\n\n**Medicaid MCO**: Managed Care Organization under contract with a state Medicaid program to deliver comprehensive Medicaid services. As of 2024, 41 states + DC use MCOs; 75%+ of all Medicaid beneficiaries are enrolled in managed care.\n\n**KLAS Market Share**: KLAS Research tracks EHR market share by number of hospitals, percentage of beds, and contract activity. This is the industry standard for EHR competitive positioning.\n\n---\n\n## Methods and Protocols\n\n**Market sizing methods applicable to each domain:**\n\n1. **Top-down (analyst reports)**: Use published market size figures as starting points. Note: analyst reports vary widely — use multiple sources and triangulate.\n\n2. **Bottom-up (unit economics)**: Multiply customer counts (from CMS, AHA, KFF) by average spending benchmarks (from HFMA, Definitive Healthcare, Bain/KLAS). More defensible than top-down for investor audiences.\n\n3. **Competitor benchmarking**: Use public revenue figures (R1 RCM $2.46B, Waystar ~$900M, Epic estimated $5B+ revenue) to bound market estimates.\n\n4. **Enrollment-based (payer domains)**: Use CMS enrollment data as the universe, then apply per-member-per-month technology spend assumptions.\n\n**Triangulation protocol**: For any market segment, use at minimum:\n- 1 analyst top-down figure\n- 1 government enrollment/utilization dataset\n- 1 public company revenue anchor\n\n---\n\n## Source Stack\n\n### DOMAIN 1: PAYER (Health Insurance Technology)\n\n---\n\n#### 1.1 Claims Management & Adjudication Technology\n\n| Source | URL | Data Type | Free/Paid | Currency | Sizing Use |\n\n---\n\n## Synthesis\n\n### Domain 1: Payer — What the Data Tells Us\n\nThe payer technology market is definitionally ambiguous across reports, but the free government data (CMS enrollment files, KFF trackers) gives us a credible customer universe:\n- **MA market**: 34M+ enrollees, 500+ plans, top 5 insurers hold 70%+ of enrollees — a concentrated market where 20-30 enterprise relationships cover most of the opportunity.\n- **Medicaid MCO**: 61.7M enrollees across 41+ state programs — a larger but more fragmented market with state government as the procurement layer.\n- **Claims management tech**: $12B–$19B TAM with CAGR ~7%. The PA automation sub-segment is faster-growing ($2.2B–$4.1B, CAGR 13–18%) and is directly regulated into growth by CMS-0057-F.\n- **Risk adjustment**: No clean analyst market exists, but the $140B CMS payment pool creates a large economic stake. Technology vendors who improve HCC coding capture a share of that pool.\n\n**Bottom-up check**: 34M MA enrollees x $X/member/year technology spend. If payers spend $5–10 PMPY on analytics/tech, that's $170M–$340M for MA analytics alone. A plausible SAM for a focused Oracle Health MA analytics product.\n\n### Domain 2: RCM — What the Data Tells Us\n\nRCM is the most data-rich domain for benchmarks. The wide analyst market range ($58B–$344B) is a methodology problem, not a reality problem. The defensible approach:\n- Use MarketsandMarkets $58B–$65B for technology-focused RCM TAM.\n- Use R1 RCM ($2.46B) and Waystar (~$900M) as competitor anchors showing that outsourced + software RCM is already multi-billion at the top tier.\n- Use HFMA MAP Key benchmarks to construct unit economics: 6,100 hospitals with avg denial rate 11.8% creates a quantifiable revenue leakage problem.\n\n**Unit economics check**: If a hospital has $100M in net patient revenue (NPR) and an 11.8% denial rate, that's ~$11.8M in claims at risk. Technology that captures even 20% of that recovery is worth $2.4M/hospital/year. Across 6,100 hospitals = $14.6B potential technology value. This supports the MarketsandMarkets $58B figure (software + services).\n\n### Domain 3: Provider / EHR — What the Data Tells Us\n\nThe EHR market is effectively saturated (96% hospital adoption). This means:\n- Growth comes from replacement contracts (Oracle losing 74 hospitals in 2024 is a red flag) and upsell into adjacent modules.\n- Hospital IT spend of $10.5M avg across 6,100 hospitals = $64B total market — EHR is ~15% of that.\n- **Ambient AI documentation** ($600M in 2025, 2.4x growth) is the highest-growth adjacent opportunity and Oracle Health (via DAX integration with Nuance/Microsoft) has direct access to this market.\n- **CDSS** ($5.79B, CAGR 11%) is a natural EHR upsell — embedded in workflows rather than standalone.\n\n---\n\n## Open Unknowns\n\n1. **Per-member-per-year payer technology spend**: No publicly available figure for PMPY technology budget at MA plans or Medicaid MCOs. This would allow a cleaner bottom-up TAM model.\n\n2. **Oracle Health revenue by segment**: Oracle does not break out Cerner/Oracle Health revenue separately in public SEC filings — makes it hard to anchor the TAM from Oracle's own position.\n\n3. **KLAS full report data**: The detailed KLAS EHR market share and IT spending reports are paid-only. The free blog summaries give top-line figures but not segment breakdowns (by bed size, state, system type).\n\n4. **Definitive Healthcare deep hospital data**: More granular hospital-level IT spending by department (RCM vs. EHR vs. analytics) requires a paid subscription.\n\n5. **Star Ratings technology market**: No standalone analyst market report found for Star Ratings optimization technology as a distinct segment. It is typically buried inside payer analytics market reports.\n\n6. **Post-OBBBA denial dynamics**: HFMA's most recent article (2026) references new denial management pressures under the \"OBBBA era\" — this regulatory context needs further research to assess technology market implications.\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Next Research Steps\n\n1. **Retrieve KLAS free blog posts for EHR 2025 data**: The KLAS engage blog (engage.klasresearch.com) publishes free summaries of key reports. Specifically pull the 2025 acute care EHR market share blog post for updated Oracle Health figures.\n\n2. **Pull KFF Medicaid MCO enrollment by plan**: The KFF Medicaid MCO tracker has state-by-state enrollment by parent firm — this is essential for identifying the 10–15 enterprise MCO relationships that represent most of the Medicaid technology TAM.\n\n3. **Access CMS MA enrollment data directly**: cms.gov monthly enrollment files are free and give exact plan-level enrollment. Download the February 2025 file for the most current count.\n\n4. **Model the PMPY approach for payer TAM**: Research Bain/KLAS payer IT spending benchmarks to find a per-member spend figure. Even $5–15 PMPY would allow a clean bottom-up model across MA (34M) and Medicaid MCO (61.7M) universes.\n\n5. **Find CodaMetrix/AI coding company revenue data**: CodaMetrix is a key pure-play AI coding vendor. Find any funding announcements or revenue disclosures to anchor the AI coding market from a vendor perspective.\n\n6. **Pull Menlo Ventures Healthcare AI report in full**: The Menlo Ventures \"State of AI in Healthcare 2025\" report contains the most credible ambient scribes market data ($600M, vendor shares). Download and read the full report.\n\n7. **HFMA MAP Key benchmarks purchase**: If a formal market sizing deliverable is needed, the HFMA MAP Key database provides the most credible RCM benchmarks and is worth purchasing for the unit economics model.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":"tool_use","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2010,"cache_read_input_tokens":59953,"output_tokens":12923,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2010},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZHdhfJXQ32Z4jrWcAsCH","type":"assistant","uuid":"f13b4818-4165-48fc-b062-e4ff74eaadd2","timestamp":"2026-03-22T06:23:16.650Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS","sessionId":"fe36a5fb-a2bc-4eb6-b6f8-8a2ba119fc51","version":"2.1.78","gitBranch":"main","slug":"federated-percolating-pnueli"}

You can save it manually or grant Write access and I'll write it to disk.\n\n---\n\n# Research Packet: Oracle Health Market Sizing Data Sources\n\n**Date**: 2026-03-22\n**Researcher**: Research Agent\n**Evidence basis**: 18 web searches across CMS, KFF, KLAS, AHA, HFMA, Grand View Research, MarketsandMarkets, Mordor Intelligence, Menlo Ventures, Bain/KLAS, Gartner, Definitive Healthcare, and public company SEC filings\n\n---\n\n## Research Question\n\nWhat publicly available market sizing data sources — containing actual enrollment counts, market size figures, spending benchmarks, and competitive revenue data — exist for Oracle Health's three primary domains: Payer technology, Revenue Cycle Management technology, and Provider / EHR technology?\n\n---\n\n## Scope Boundaries\n\n**In scope**: Government enrollment datasets (free), market research reports (free abstracts or paid), public company SEC filings, industry association benchmarks, analyst firm estimates.\n\n**Out of scope**: Proprietary primary research, consulting firm deliverables not available publicly, internal Oracle Health data.\n\n**SAM/SOM excluded**: This packet is inputs only — not the sizing model itself.\n\n---\n\n## Canonical Definitions\n\n**TAM (Top-Down)**: Total market size from analyst reports. Used as ceiling estimate.\n\n**TAM (Bottom-Up)**: (Number of customers) x (Average spend per customer). More defensible. Requires both a customer count source and a spending benchmark source.\n\n**Competitor benchmark method**: Infer market size from sum of known public company revenues.\n\n**Replacement market**: When adoption is saturated (>95%), all new contracts come at a competitor's expense. EHR market is a replacement market.\n\n**CMS-0057-F**: The CMS Interoperability and Prior Authorization Final Rule (Jan 17, 2024), which mandates FHIR-based PA APIs for MA plans, Medicaid MCOs, and CHIP — a regulatory forcing function for PA automation technology.\n\n**KLAS market share**: Industry standard for EHR competitive tracking. Measured by hospital count, bed-weighted share, and net contract gains/losses.\n\n---\n\n## Methods and Protocols\n\nThree sizing methods apply across these domains:\n\n**Method 1 — Top-Down (analyst reports)**: Use published TAM figures as starting points. Always triangulate across 3+ sources because methodology differences create wide variance. The right estimate is usually in the middle of the range.\n\n**Method 2 — Bottom-Up (unit economics)**: Multiply customer universe (from CMS, AHA, KFF) by spending benchmarks (from HFMA, Definitive Healthcare). More defensible for investor audiences.\n\n**Method 3 — Competitor anchoring**: Use public company revenues (R1 RCM $2.46B, Waystar ~$900M run-rate, ambient scribes $600M) to bound the market from the supply side.\n\n**Triangulation requirement**: For any market segment, use at minimum one analyst figure, one government enrollment/utilization anchor, and one public company revenue anchor.\n\n---\n\n## Source Stack\n\n### DOMAIN 1: PAYER (Health Insurance Technology)\n\n---\n\n#### 1.1 Claims Management & Adjudication Technology\n\n| Source | URL | Data | Free/Paid | Currency | Sizing Method |\n|--------|-----|------|-----------|----------|---------------|\n| Mordor Intelligence — Healthcare Claims Management | mordorintelligence.com/industry-reports/healthcare-claims-management-market | Payers managed 53.7% of total claims in 2025; | 33% | Menlo Ventures |\n| Abridge ambient market share | 30% | Menlo Ventures |\n| CDSS market | $2.5B–$10.75B (2024) | Multiple |\n\n---\n\n## Synthesis\n\n### What the data actually says about each domain:\n\n**Payer**: Free government data (CMS enrollment files, KFF) provides the best customer universe. Market is concentrated — 20-30 enterprise relationships at the top MA/Medicaid MCO payers represent the majority of the addressable opportunity. PA automation is the highest-urgency sub-market due to CMS-0057-F regulatory mandate. Risk adjustment technology TAM is best derived from the $140B CMS payment pool, not from software market reports.\n\n**RCM**: The most benchmark-rich domain. HFMA MAP Keys provide the industry standard for RCM performance benchmarking. The $58B MarketsandMarkets figure (technology-focused) is the right TAM anchor; ignore $300B+ figures that include all hospital financial operations. R1 RCM ($2.46B) and Waystar (~$900M) anchor the competitive supply side. Denial rate deteriorating to 11.8% in 2024 is the primary demand driver.\n\n**Provider/EHR**: Market is saturated (96% EHR adoption) — this is a replacement/upgrade market. Oracle Health's -74 hospital net loss in 2024 is a strategic signal, not a data point to explain away. Ambient AI documentation ($600M in 2025, 2.4x growth) is the highest-growth adjacent opportunity. Hospital IT spend benchmarks (avg $10.5M/hospital, 2.3% of operating expense) enable clean bottom-up modeling.\n\n### Bottom-up validation checks:\n- **Hospital IT market**: 6,100 hospitals x $10.5M = $64B total hospital IT. EHR at ~15% = $9.6B. Matches $9.9B projection.\n- **RCM opportunity**: 6,100 hospitals, avg $100M NPR, 11.8% denial rate = $11.8M at-risk per hospital. Technology capturing 20% of recovery = $2.4M/hospital/year. Across 6,100 hospitals = $14.6B technology value. Supports MarketsandMarkets $58B figure (tech + services combined).\n- **MA payer market**: 34M enrollees, top 5 payers hold 70%+ — treat as enterprise software market with 10-20 accounts controlling most spend.\n\n---\n\n## Open Unknowns\n\n1. **Per-member-per-year payer technology spend**: No public figure found for PMPY technology budget at MA plans or Medicaid MCOs. Bain/KLAS paid report likely contains this.\n\n2. **Oracle Health revenue by segment**: Oracle Corp does not break out Oracle Health revenue in SEC filings — making it impossible to anchor Oracle's installed base value from public data alone.\n\n3. **Star Ratings technology as a standalone market**: No clean analyst report found for Star Ratings optimization technology as a distinct segment. Buried in payer analytics reports.\n\n4. **Post-OBBBA denial dynamics**: HFMA's most recent material (referenced in search) discusses new denial pressures under the \"OBBBA era\" — needs direct reading to understand technology demand implications.\n\n5. **KLAS full report data**: Segment breakdowns by bed size, state, and system type require the paid KLAS report. Free summaries give top-line share only.\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Next Research Steps\n\n1. **Download CMS MA enrollment file directly** — cms.gov monthly enrollment CSVs are free and give plan-level data. Pull February 2025 for current state.\n\n2. **Pull KFF Medicaid MCO tracker by parent firm** — identifies the 15-20 enterprise MCO relationships that represent most of the Medicaid technology TAM.\n\n3. **Read Menlo Ventures Healthcare AI 2025 report in full** — best single free source on ambient AI market. Confirms DAX share, growth rate, and vendor competitive dynamics.\n\n4. **Access KLAS 2025 EHR blog post for updated Oracle Health figures** — engage.klasresearch.com publishes free blog summaries of reports.\n\n5. **Model PMPY approach for payer TAM** — use Bain/KLAS paid report or primary research to find per-member IT spend; apply to 34M MA + 61.7M Medicaid MCO universe.\n\n6. **Pull HFMA MAP Key database for unit economics** — if a formal deliverable is needed, HFMA MAP Key benchmarks are the most defensible RCM inputs available. Worth purchasing.\n\n7. **Find CodaMetrix funding/revenue disclosures** — pure-play AI coding vendor. Any funding announcement or customer case study with ACV data anchors the AI coding sub-market from the vendor side.\n\n---\n\n**Confidence tier**: AUTO — sources are confirmed public, links are valid, figures are attributed.\n**Context health**: GREEN\n**Evidence basis**: 18 web searches covering CMS, KFF, MedPAC, ONC, AHA, HFMA, KLAS, MarketsandMarkets, Grand View Research, Mordor Intelligence, IMARC, Menlo Ventures, Bain, Gartner, Definitive Healthcare, StockAnalysis, and public SEC filings.\n**Next step**: Decide which domains need a full bottom-up model vs. which can use top-down figures — then pull the specific free government data (CMS enrollment CSVs, ONC dashboard, AHA Fast Facts) as the unit economics inputs."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":13087,"cache_read_input_tokens":61963,"output_tokens":11338,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":13087},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZHdzmFvnNoHNgH4h6mpZ","type":"assistant","uuid":"58b1b9ef-3bcd-49c8-a3ed-2fc34fb54f69","timestamp":"2026-03-22T06:26:47.188Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-desktop","cwd":"/Users/mikerodgers/Startup-Intelligence-OS","sessionId":"fe36a5fb-a2bc-4eb6-b6f8-8a2ba119fc51","version":"2.1.78","gitBranch":"main","slug":"federated-percolating-pnueli"}
